      29             : /*
      30             :  *
      31             :  * This file is a C translation of the Fortran code known as QUADPACK written by
      32             :  * R. Piessens, E. de Doncker-Kapenga, C. Überhuber , and D. Kahaner with the
      33             :  * original description below.
      34             :  *
      35             :  */
      36             : 
      37             : /* * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * *
      38             :  *
      39             :  * QUADPACK is a FORTRAN subroutine package for the numerical
      40             :  * computation of definite one-dimensional integrals. It originated
      41             :  * from a joint project of R. Piessens and E. de Doncker (Appl.
      42             :  * Math. and Progr. Div.- K.U.Leuven, Belgium), C. Ueberhuber (Inst.
      43             :  * Fuer Math.- Techn.U.Wien, Austria), and D. Kahaner (Nation. Bur.
      44             :  * of Standards- Washington D.C., U.S.A.).
      45             :  * The routine names for the DOUBLE PRECISION versions are preceded
      46             :  * by the letter D.
      47             :  *
      48             :  * - QNG  : Is a simple non-adaptive automatic integrator, based on
      49             :  *          a sequence of rules with increasing degree of algebraic
      50             :  *          precision (Patterson, 1968).
      51             :  *
      52             :  * - QAG  : Is a simple globally adaptive integrator using the
      53             :  *          strategy of Aind (Piessens, 1973). It is possible to
      54             :  *          choose between 6 pairs of Gauss-Kronrod quadrature
      55             :  *          formulae for the rule evaluation component. The pairs
      56             :  *          of high degree of precision are suitable for handling
      57             :  *          integration difficulties due to a strongly oscillating
      58             :  *          integrand.
      59             :  *
      60             :  * - QAGS : Is an integrator based on globally adaptive interval
      61             :  *          subdivision in connection with extrapolation (de Doncker,
      62             :  *          1978) by the Epsilon algorithm (Wynn, 1956).
      63             :  *
      64             :  * - QAGP : Serves the same purposes as QAGS, but also allows
      65             :  *          for eventual user-supplied information, i.e. the
      66             :  *          abscissae of internal singularities, discontinuities
      67             :  *          and other difficulties of the integrand function.
      68             :  *          The algorithm is a modification of that in QAGS.
      69             :  *
      70             :  * - QAGI : Handles integration over infinite intervals. The
      71             :  *          infinite range is mapped onto a finite interval and
      72             :  *          then the same strategy as in QAGS is applied.
      73             :  *
      74             :  * - QAWO : Is a routine for the integration of COS(OMEGA*X)*F(X)
      75             :  *          or SIN(OMEGA*X)*F(X) over a finite interval (A,B).
      76             :  *          OMEGA is specified by the user
      77             :  *          The rule evaluation component is based on the
      78             :  *          modified Clenshaw-Curtis technique.
      79             :  *          An adaptive subdivision scheme is used connected with
      80             :  *          an extrapolation procedure, which is a modification
      81             :  *          of that in QAGS and provides the possibility to deal
      82             :  *          even with singularities in F.
      83             :  *
      84             :  * - QAWF : Calculates the Fourier cosine or Fourier sine
      85             :  *          transform of F(X), for user-supplied interval (A,
      86             :  *          INFINITY), OMEGA, and F. The procedure of QAWO is
      87             :  *          used on successive finite intervals, and convergence
      88             :  *          acceleration by means of the Epsilon algorithm (Wynn,
      89             :  *          1956) is applied to the series of the integral
      90             :  *          contributions.
      91             :  *
      92             :  * - QAWS : Integrates W(X)*F(X) over (A,B) with A.LT.B finite,
      93             :  *          and   W(X) = ((X-A)**ALFA)*((B-X)**BETA)*V(X)
      94             :  *          where V(X) = 1 or LOG(X-A) or LOG(B-X)
      95             :  *                         or LOG(X-A)*LOG(B-X)
      96             :  *          and   ALFA.GT.(-1), BETA.GT.(-1).
      97             :  *          The user specifies A, B, ALFA, BETA and the type of
      98             :  *          the function V.
      99             :  *          A globally adaptive subdivision strategy is applied,
     100             :  *          with modified Clenshaw-Curtis integration on the
     101             :  *          subintervals which contain A or B.
     102             :  *
     103             :  * - QAWC : Computes the Cauchy Principal Value of F(X)/(X-C)
     104             :  *          over a finite interval (A,B) and for
     105             :  *          user-determined C.
     106             :  *          The strategy is globally adaptive, and modified
     107             :  *          Clenshaw-Curtis integration is used on the subranges
     108             :  *          which contain the point X = C.
     109             :  *
     110             :  *    Each of the routines above also has a "more detailed" version
     111             :  * with a name ending in E, as QAGE.  These provide more
     112             :  * information and control than the easier versions.
     113             :  *
     114             :  *
     115             :  *    The preceding routines are all automatic.  That is, the user
     116             :  * inputs his problem and an error tolerance.  The routine
     117             :  * attempts to perform the integration to within the requested
     118             :  * absolute or relative error.
     119             :  *    There are, in addition, a number of non-automatic integrators.
     120             :  * These are most useful when the problem is such that the
     121             :  * user knows that a fixed rule will provide the accuracy
     122             :  * required.  Typically they return an error estimate but make
     123             :  * no attempt to satisfy any particular input error request.
     124             :  *
     125             :  *   QK15 QK21 QK31 QK41 QK51 QK61
     126             :  *        Estimate the integral on [a,b] using 15, 21,..., 61
     127             :  *        point rule and return an error estimate.
     128             :  *   QK15I 15 point rule for (semi)infinite interval.
     129             :  *   QK15W 15 point rule for special singular weight functions.
     130             :  *   QC25C 25 point rule for Cauchy Principal Values
     131             :  *   QC25F 25 point rule for sin/cos integrand.
     132             :  *   QMOMO Integrates k-th degree Chebychev polynomial times
     133             :  *         function with various explicit singularities.
     134             :  *
     135             :  * Support functions from linpack, slatec, and blas have been omitted
     136             :  * by default but can be obtained by asking.  For example, suppose you
     137             :  * already have installed linpack and the blas, but not slatec.  Then
     138             :  * use a request like  "send dqag from quadpack slatec".
     139             :  *
     140             :  *
     141             :  * [see also toms/691]
     142             :  * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * *
     143             :  *
     144             :  * The original Fortran code can be found at https://www.netlib.org/quadpack/
     145             :  *
     146             :  * References:
     147             :  *
     148             :  * [1]: Robert Piessens, Elise Doncker-Kapenga, Christoph Überhuber, David
     149             :  *      Kahaner. "QUADPACK: A subroutine package for automatic integration",
     150             :  *      Springer, 1983, https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-642-61786-7
     151             :  *
     152             :  *
     153             :  * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * * */
     154             :

     195             : void
     196      112393 : dqagie(double(*fcn)(double* x), const double bound, const int inf,
     197             :        const double epsabs, const double epsrel, const int limit, double* result,
     198             :        double* abserr, int* neval, int* ier, double* alist, double* blist,
     199             :        double* rlist, double* elist, int* iord, int* last)
     200      111373 : {
     201             :     // ***begin prologue  dqagie
     202             :     // ***date written   800101   (yymmdd)
     203             :     // ***revision date  830518   (yymmdd)
     204             :     // ***category no.  h2a3a1,h2a4a1
     205             :     // ***keywords  automatic integrator, infinite intervals,
     206             :     //              general-purpose, transformation, extrapolation,
     207             :     //              globally adaptive
     208             :     // ***author  piessens,robert,appl. math & progr. div - k.u.leuven
     209             :     //            de doncker,elise,appl. math & progr. div - k.u.leuven
     210             :     // ***purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a given
     211             :     //             integral   i = integral of f over (bound,+infinity)
     212             :     //             or i = integral of f over (-infinity,bound)
     213             :     //             or i = integral of f over (-infinity,+infinity),
     214             :     //             hopefully satisfying following claim for accuracy
     215             :     //             abs(i-result).le.max(epsabs,epsrel*abs(i))
     216             :     // ***description
     217             :     //
     218             :     //  integration over infinite intervals
     219             :     //  standard fortran subroutine
     220             :     //
     221             :     //             f      - double precision
     222             :     //                      function subprogram defining the integrand
     223             :     //                      function f(x). the actual name for f needs to be
     224             :     //                      declared e x t e r n a l in the driver program.
     225             :     //
     226             :     //             bound  - double precision
     227             :     //                      finite bound of integration range
     228             :     //                      (has no meaning if interval is doubly-infinite)
     229             :     //
     230             :     //             inf    - double precision
     231             :     //                      indicating the kind of integration range involved
     232             :     //                      inf = 1 corresponds to  (bound,+infinity),
     233             :     //                      inf = -1            to  (-infinity,bound),
     234             :     //                      inf = 2             to (-infinity,+infinity).
     235             :     //
     236             :     //             epsabs - double precision
     237             :     //                      absolute accuracy requested
     238             :     //             epsrel - double precision
     239             :     //                      relative accuracy requested
     240             :     //                      if  epsabs.le.0
     241             :     //                      and epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
     242             :     //                      the routine will end with ier = 6.
     243             :     //
     244             :     //             limit  - integer
     245             :     //                      gives an upper bound on the number of subintervals
     246             :     //                      in the partition of (a,b), limit.ge.1
     247             :     //
     248             :     //          on return
     249             :     //             result - double precision
     250             :     //                      approximation to the integral
     251             :     //
     252             :     //             abserr - double precision
     253             :     //                      estimate of the modulus of the absolute error,
     254             :     //                      which should equal or exceed abs(i-result)
     255             :     //
     256             :     //             neval  - integer
     257             :     //                      number of integrand evaluations
     258             :     //
     259             :     //             ier    - integer
     260             :     //                      ier = 0 normal and reliable termination of the
     261             :     //                              routine. it is assumed that the requested
     262             :     //                              accuracy has been achieved.
     263             :     //                    - ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine. the
     264             :     //                              estimates for result and error are less
     265             :     //                              reliable. it is assumed that the requested
     266             :     //                              accuracy has not been achieved.
     267             :     //             error messages
     268             :     //                      ier = 1 maximum number of subdivisions allowed
     269             :     //                              has been achieved. one can allow more
     270             :     //                              subdivisions by increasing the value of
     271             :     //                              limit (and taking the according dimension
     272             :     //                              adjustments into account). however,if
     273             :     //                              this yields no improvement it is advised
     274             :     //                              to analyze the integrand in order to
     275             :     //                              determine the integration difficulties.
     276             :     //                              if the position of a local difficulty can
     277             :     //                              be determined (e.g. singularity,
     278             :     //                              discontinuity within the interval) one
     279             :     //                              will probably gain from splitting up the
     280             :     //                              interval at this point and calling the
     281             :     //                              integrator on the subranges. if possible,
     282             :     //                              an appropriate special-purpose integrator
     283             :     //                              should be used, which is designed for
     284             :     //                              handling the type of difficulty involved.
     285             :     //                          = 2 the occurrence of roundoff error is
     286             :     //                              detected, which prevents the requested
     287             :     //                              tolerance from being achieved.
     288             :     //                              the error may be under-estimated.
     289             :     //                          = 3 extremely bad integrand behaviour occurs
     290             :     //                              at some points of the integration
     291             :     //                              interval.
     292             :     //                          = 4 the algorithm does not converge.
     293             :     //                              roundoff error is detected in the
     294             :     //                              extrapolation table.
     295             :     //                              it is assumed that the requested tolerance
     296             :     //                              cannot be achieved, and that the returned
     297             :     //                              result is the best which can be obtained.
     298             :     //                          = 5 the integral is probably divergent, or
     299             :     //                              slowly convergent. it must be noted that
     300             :     //                              divergence can occur with any other value
     301             :     //                              of ier.
     302             :     //                          = 6 the input is invalid, because
     303             :     //                              (epsabs.le.0 and
     304             :     //                               epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
     305             :     //                              result, abserr, neval, last, rlist(1),
     306             :     //                              elist(1) and iord(1) are set to zero.
     307             :     //                              alist(1) and blist(1) are set to 0
     308             :     //                              and 1 respectively.
     309             :     //
     310             :     //             alist  - double precision
     311             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     312             :     //                       last  elements of which are the left
     313             :     //                      end points of the subintervals in the partition
     314             :     //                      of the transformed integration range (0,1).
     315             :     //
     316             :     //             blist  - double precision
     317             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     318             :     //                       last  elements of which are the right
     319             :     //                      end points of the subintervals in the partition
     320             :     //                      of the transformed integration range (0,1).
     321             :     //
     322             :     //             rlist  - double precision
     323             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     324             :     //                       last  elements of which are the integral
     325             :     //                      approximations on the subintervals
     326             :     //
     327             :     //             elist  - double precision
     328             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit,  the first
     329             :     //                      last elements of which are the moduli of the
     330             :     //                      absolute error estimates on the subintervals
     331             :     //
     332             :     //             iord   - integer
     333             :     //                      vector of dimension limit, the first k
     334             :     //                      elements of which are pointers to the
     335             :     //                      error estimates over the subintervals,
     336             :     //                      such that elist(iord(1)), ..., elist(iord(k))
     337             :     //                      form a decreasing sequence, with k = last
     338             :     //                      if last.le.(limit/2+2), and k = limit+1-last
     339             :     //                      otherwise
     340             :     //
     341             :     //             last   - integer
     342             :     //                      number of subintervals actually produced
     343             :     //                      in the subdivision process
     344             :     //
     345             :     // ***references  (none)
     346             :     // ***routines called  d1mach,dqelg,dqk15i,dqpsrt
     347             :     // ***end prologue  dqagie
     348             :     //
     349             :     //             the dimension of rlist2 is determined by the value of
     350             :     //             limexp in subroutine dqelg.
     351             :     //
     352             :     //
     353             :     //             list of major variables
     354             :     //             -----------------------
     355             :     //
     356             :     //            alist     - list of left end points of all subintervals
     357             :     //                        considered up to now
     358             :     //            blist     - list of right end points of all subintervals
     359             :     //                        considered up to now
     360             :     //            rlist(i)  - approximation to the integral over
     361             :     //                        (alist(i),blist(i))
     362             :     //            rlist2    - array of dimension at least (limexp+2),
     363             :     //                        containing the part of the epsilon table
     364             :     //                        which is still needed for further computations
     365             :     //            elist(i)  - error estimate applying to rlist(i)
     366             :     //            maxerr    - pointer to the interval with largest error
     367             :     //                        estimate
     368             :     //            errmax    - elist(maxerr)
     369             :     //            erlast    - error on the interval currently subdivided
     370             :     //                        (before that subdivision has taken place)
     371             :     //            area      - sum of the integrals over the subintervals
     372             :     //            errsum    - sum of the errors over the subintervals
     373             :     //            errbnd    - requested accuracy max(epsabs,epsrel*
     374             :     //                        abs(result))
     375             :     //            *****1    - variable for the left subinterval
     376             :     //            *****2    - variable for the right subinterval
     377             :     //            last      - index for subdivision
     378             :     //            nres      - number of calls to the extrapolation routine
     379             :     //            numrl2    - number of elements currently in rlist2. if an
     380             :     //                        appropriate approximation to the compounded
     381             :     //                        integral has been obtained, it is put in
     382             :     //                        rlist2(numrl2) after numrl2 has been increased
     383             :     //                        by one.
     384             :     //            small     - length of the smallest interval considered up
     385             :     //                        to now, multiplied by 1.5
     386             :     //            erlarg    - sum of the errors over the intervals larger
     387             :     //                        than the smallest interval considered up to now
     388             :     //            extrap    - logical variable denoting that the routine
     389             :     //                        is attempting to perform extrapolation. i.e.
     390             :     //                        before subdividing the smallest interval we
     391             :     //                        try to decrease the value of erlarg.
     392             :     //            noext     - logical variable denoting that extrapolation
     393             :     //                        is no longer allowed (true-value)
     394             :     //
     395             :     //             machine dependent constants
     396             :     //             ---------------------------
     397             :     //
     398             :     //            epmach is the largest relative spacing.
     399             :     //            uflow is the smallest positive magnitude.
     400             :     //            oflow is the largest positive magnitude.
     401             :     //

     425             :     // first approximation to the integral
     426             :     // -----------------------------------
     427             :     // determine the interval to be mapped onto (0,1).
     428             :     // if inf = 2 the integral is computed as i = i1+i2, where

     431             :

     626             : 
     627             : void
     628       19119 : dqagpe(double(*fcn)(double* x), const double a, const double b, int npts2,
     629             :        double* points, const double epsabs, const double epsrel, const int limit,
     630             :        double* result, double* abserr, int* neval, int* ier, double* alist,
     631             :        double* blist, double* rlist, double* elist, double* pts, int* iord,
     632             :        int* level, int* ndin, int* last)
     633             : {
     634             :     // ***begin prologue  dqagpe
     635             :     // ***date written   800101   (yymmdd)
     636             :     // ***revision date  830518   (yymmdd)
     637             :     // ***category no.  h2a2a1
     638             :     // ***keywords  automatic integrator, general-purpose,
     639             :     //              singularities at user specified points,
     640             :     //              extrapolation, globally adaptive.
     641             :     // ***author  piessens,robert ,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
     642             :     //            de doncker,elise,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
     643             :     // ***purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a given
     644             :     //             definite integral i = integral of f over (a,b), hopefully
     645             :     //             satisfying following claim for accuracy abs(i-result).le.
     646             :     //             max(epsabs,epsrel*abs(i)). break points of the integration
     647             :     //             interval, where local difficulties of the integrand may
     648             :     //             occur(e.g. singularities,discontinuities),provided by user.
     649             :     // ***description
     650             :     //
     651             :     //         computation of a definite integral
     652             :     //         standard fortran subroutine
     653             :     //         double precision version
     654             :     //
     655             :     //         parameters
     656             :     //          on entry
     657             :     //             f      - double precision
     658             :     //                      function subprogram defining the integrand
     659             :     //                      function f(x). the actual name for f needs to be
     660             :     //                      declared e x t e r n a l in the driver program.
     661             :     //
     662             :     //             a      - double precision
     663             :     //                      lower limit of integration
     664             :     //
     665             :     //             b      - double precision
     666             :     //                      upper limit of integration
     667             :     //
     668             :     //             npts2  - integer
     669             :     //                      number equal to two more than the number of
     670             :     //                      user-supplied break points within the integration
     671             :     //                      range, npts2.ge.2.
     672             :     //                      if npts2.lt.2, the routine will end with ier = 6.
     673             :     //
     674             :     //             points - double precision
     675             :     //                      vector of dimension npts2, the first (npts2-2)
     676             :     //                      elements of which are the user provided break
     677             :     //                      points. if these points do not constitute an
     678             :     //                      ascending sequence there will be an automatic
     679             :     //                      sorting.
     680             :     //
     681             :     //             epsabs - double precision
     682             :     //                      absolute accuracy requested
     683             :     //             epsrel - double precision
     684             :     //                      relative accuracy requested
     685             :     //                      if  epsabs.le.0
     686             :     //                      and epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
     687             :     //                      the routine will end with ier = 6.
     688             :     //
     689             :     //             limit  - integer
     690             :     //                      gives an upper bound on the number of subintervals
     691             :     //                      in the partition of (a,b), limit.ge.npts2
     692             :     //                      if limit.lt.npts2, the routine will end with
     693             :     //                      ier = 6.
     694             :     //
     695             :     //          on return
     696             :     //             result - double precision
     697             :     //                      approximation to the integral
     698             :     //
     699             :     //             abserr - double precision
     700             :     //                      estimate of the modulus of the absolute error,
     701             :     //                      which should equal or exceed abs(i-result)
     702             :     //
     703             :     //             neval  - integer
     704             :     //                      number of integrand evaluations
     705             :     //
     706             :     //             ier    - integer
     707             :     //                      ier = 0 normal and reliable termination of the
     708             :     //                              routine. it is assumed that the requested
     709             :     //                              accuracy has been achieved.
     710             :     //                      ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine.
     711             :     //                              the estimates for integral and error are
     712             :     //                              less reliable. it is assumed that the
     713             :     //                              requested accuracy has not been achieved.
     714             :     //             error messages
     715             :     //                      ier = 1 maximum number of subdivisions allowed
     716             :     //                              has been achieved. one can allow more
     717             :     //                              subdivisions by increasing the value of
     718             :     //                              limit (and taking the according dimension
     719             :     //                              adjustments into account). however, if
     720             :     //                              this yields no improvement it is advised
     721             :     //                              to analyze the integrand in order to
     722             :     //                              determine the integration difficulties. if
     723             :     //                              the position of a local difficulty can be
     724             :     //                              determined (i.e. singularity,
     725             :     //                              discontinuity within the interval), it
     726             :     //                              should be supplied to the routine as an
     727             :     //                              element of the vector points. if necessary
     728             :     //                              an appropriate special-purpose integrator
     729             :     //                              must be used, which is designed for
     730             :     //                              handling the type of difficulty involved.
     731             :     //                          = 2 the occurrence of roundoff error is
     732             :     //                              detected, which prevents the requested
     733             :     //                              tolerance from being achieved.
     734             :     //                              the error may be under-estimated.
     735             :     //                          = 3 extremely bad integrand behaviour occurs
     736             :     //                              at some points of the integration
     737             :     //                              interval.
     738             :     //                          = 4 the algorithm does not converge.
     739             :     //                              roundoff error is detected in the
     740             :     //                              extrapolation table. it is presumed that
     741             :     //                              the requested tolerance cannot be
     742             :     //                              achieved, and that the returned result is
     743             :     //                              the best which can be obtained.
     744             :     //                          = 5 the integral is probably divergent, or
     745             :     //                              slowly convergent. it must be noted that
     746             :     //                              divergence can occur with any other value
     747             :     //                              of ier.gt.0.
     748             :     //                          = 6 the input is invalid because
     749             :     //                              npts2.lt.2 or
     750             :     //                              break points are specified outside
     751             :     //                              the integration range or
     752             :     //                              (epsabs.le.0 and
     753             :     //                               epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28))
     754             :     //                              or limit.lt.npts2.
     755             :     //                              result, abserr, neval, last, rlist(1),
     756             :     //                              and elist(1) are set to zero. alist(1) and
     757             :     //                              blist(1) are set to a and b respectively.
     758             :     //
     759             :     //             alist  - double precision
     760             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     761             :     //                       last  elements of which are the left end points
     762             :     //                      of the subintervals in the partition of the given
     763             :     //                      integration range (a,b)
     764             :     //
     765             :     //             blist  - double precision
     766             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     767             :     //                       last  elements of which are the right end points
     768             :     //                      of the subintervals in the partition of the given
     769             :     //                      integration range (a,b)
     770             :     //
     771             :     //             rlist  - double precision
     772             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     773             :     //                       last  elements of which are the integral
     774             :     //                      approximations on the subintervals
     775             :     //
     776             :     //             elist  - double precision
     777             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
     778             :     //                       last  elements of which are the moduli of the
     779             :     //                      absolute error estimates on the subintervals
     780             :     //
     781             :     //             pts    - double precision
     782             :     //                      vector of dimension at least npts2, containing the
     783             :     //                      integration limits and the break points of the
     784             :     //                      interval in ascending sequence.
     785             :     //
     786             :     //             level  - integer
     787             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, containing the
     788             :     //                      subdivision levels of the subinterval, i.e. if
     789             :     //                      (aa,bb) is a subinterval of (p1,p2) where p1 as
     790             :     //                      well as p2 is a user-provided break point or
     791             :     //                      integration limit, then (aa,bb) has level l if
     792             :     //                      abs(bb-aa) = abs(p2-p1)*2**(-l).
     793             :     //
     794             :     //             ndin   - integer
     795             :     //                      vector of dimension at least npts2, after first
     796             :     //                      integration over the intervals (pts(i)),pts(i+1),
     797             :     //                      i = 0,1, ..., npts2-2, the error estimates over
     798             :     //                      some of the intervals may have been increased
     799             :     //                      artificially, in order to put their subdivision
     800             :     //                      forward. if this happens for the subinterval
     801             :     //                      numbered k, ndin(k) is put to 1, otherwise
     802             :     //                      ndin(k) = 0.
     803             :     //
     804             :     //             iord   - integer
     805             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first k
     806             :     //                      elements of which are pointers to the
     807             :     //                      error estimates over the subintervals,
     808             :     //                      such that elist(iord(1)), ..., elist(iord(k))
     809             :     //                      form a decreasing sequence, with k = last
     810             :     //                      if last.le.(limit/2+2), and k = limit+1-last
     811             :     //                      otherwise
     812             :     //
     813             :     //             last   - integer
     814             :     //                      number of subintervals actually produced in the
     815             :     //                      subdivisions process
     816             :     //
     817             :     // ***references  (none)
     818             :     // ***routines called  d1mach,dqelg,dqk21,dqpsrt
     819             :     // ***end prologue  dqagpe
     820             :     //
     821             :     //             the dimension of rlist2 is determined by the value of
     822             :     //             limexp in subroutine epsalg (rlist2 should be of dimension
     823             :     //             (limexp+2) at least).
     824             :     //
     825             :     //
     826             :     //             list of major variables
     827             :     //             -----------------------
     828             :     //
     829             :     //            alist     - list of left end points of all subintervals
     830             :     //                        considered up to now
     831             :     //            blist     - list of right end points of all subintervals
     832             :     //                        considered up to now
     833             :     //            rlist(i)  - approximation to the integral over
     834             :     //                        (alist(i),blist(i))
     835             :     //            rlist2    - array of dimension at least limexp+2
     836             :     //                        containing the part of the epsilon table which
     837             :     //                        is still needed for further computations
     838             :     //            elist(i)  - error estimate applying to rlist(i)
     839             :     //            maxerr    - pointer to the interval with largest error
     840             :     //                        estimate
     841             :     //            errmax    - elist(maxerr)
     842             :     //            erlast    - error on the interval currently subdivided
     843             :     //                        (before that subdivision has taken place)
     844             :     //            area      - sum of the integrals over the subintervals
     845             :     //            errsum    - sum of the errors over the subintervals
     846             :     //            errbnd    - requested accuracy max(epsabs,epsrel*
     847             :     //                        abs(result))
     848             :     //            *****1    - variable for the left subinterval
     849             :     //            *****2    - variable for the right subinterval
     850             :     //            last      - index for subdivision
     851             :     //            nres      - number of calls to the extrapolation routine
     852             :     //            numrl2    - number of elements in rlist2. if an appropriate
     853             :     //                        approximation to the compounded integral has
     854             :     //                        been obtained, it is put in rlist2(numrl2) after
     855             :     //                        numrl2 has been increased by one.
     856             :     //            erlarg    - sum of the errors over the intervals larger
     857             :     //                        than the smallest interval considered up to now
     858             :     //            extrap    - logical variable denoting that the routine
     859             :     //                        is attempting to perform extrapolation. i.e.
     860             :     //                        before subdividing the smallest interval we
     861             :     //                        try to decrease the value of erlarg.
     862             :     //            noext     - logical variable denoting that extrapolation is
     863             :     //                        no longer allowed (true-value)
     864             :     //
     865             :     //             machine dependent constants
     866             :     //             ---------------------------
     867             :     //
     868             :     //            epmach is the largest relative spacing.
     869             :     //            uflow is the smallest positive magnitude.
     870             :     //            oflow is the largest positive magnitude.
     871             :     //
     872       19119 :     int i, ierror, ind1, ind2, iroff1, iroff2, iroff3, j, jlow,jupbnd;
     873       19119 :     int k, ksgn, ktmin, L, levcur, levmax, maxerr, nint, npts, nres, nrmax;
     874       19119 :     int numrl2, extrap, noext;
     875       19119 :     double abseps, area, area1, area12, area2, a1, a2, b1, b2, correc;
     876       19119 :     double defabs, defab1, defab2, dres, erlarg, erlast, errbnd, errmax, error1;
     877       19119 :     double error12, error2, errsum, ertest, resa, resabs, reseps, sign, temp;
     878       19119 :     double res3la[3], rlist2[52];
     879       19119 :     k = 0;
     880       19119 :     correc = 0.0;
     881             : 
     882             :     // Test validity of parameters.

    1176             : void
    1177        7762 : dqagse(double(*fcn)(double* x), const double a, const double b,
    1178             :        const double epsabs, const double epsrel, const int limit, double* result,
    1179             :        double* abserr, int* neval, int* ier, double* alist, double* blist,
    1180             :        double* rlist, double* elist, int* iord, int* last)
    1181        5965 : {
    1182             :     // ***begin prologue  dqagse
    1183             :     // ***date written   800101   (yymmdd)
    1184             :     // ***revision date  830518   (yymmdd)
    1185             :     // ***category no.  h2a1a1
    1186             :     // ***keywords  automatic integrator, general-purpose,
    1187             :     //              (end point) singularities, extrapolation,
    1188             :     //              globally adaptive
    1189             :     // ***author  piessens,robert,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    1190             :     //            de doncker,elise,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    1191             :     // ***purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a given
    1192             :     //             definite integral i = integral of f over (a,b),
    1193             :     //             hopefully satisfying following claim for accuracy
    1194             :     //             abs(i-result).le.max(epsabs,epsrel*abs(i)).
    1195             :     // ***description
    1196             :     //
    1197             :     //         computation of a definite integral
    1198             :     //         standard fortran subroutine
    1199             :     //         double precision version
    1200             :     //
    1201             :     //         parameters
    1202             :     //          on entry
    1203             :     //             f      - double precision
    1204             :     //                      function subprogram defining the integrand
    1205             :     //                      function f(x). the actual name for f needs to be
    1206             :     //                      declared e x t e r n a l in the driver program.
    1207             :     //
    1208             :     //             a      - double precision
    1209             :     //                      lower limit of integration
    1210             :     //
    1211             :     //             b      - double precision
    1212             :     //                      upper limit of integration
    1213             :     //
    1214             :     //             epsabs - double precision
    1215             :     //                      absolute accuracy requested
    1216             :     //             epsrel - double precision
    1217             :     //                      relative accuracy requested
    1218             :     //                      if  epsabs.le.0
    1219             :     //                      and epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
    1220             :     //                      the routine will end with ier = 6.
    1221             :     //
    1222             :     //             limit  - integer
    1223             :     //                      gives an upperbound on the number of subintervals
    1224             :     //                      in the partition of (a,b)
    1225             :     //
    1226             :     //          on return
    1227             :     //             result - double precision
    1228             :     //                      approximation to the integral
    1229             :     //
    1230             :     //             abserr - double precision
    1231             :     //                      estimate of the modulus of the absolute error,
    1232             :     //                      which should equal or exceed abs(i-result)
    1233             :     //
    1234             :     //             neval  - integer
    1235             :     //                      number of integrand evaluations
    1236             :     //
    1237             :     //             ier    - integer
    1238             :     //                      ier = 0 normal and reliable termination of the
    1239             :     //                              routine. it is assumed that the requested
    1240             :     //                              accuracy has been achieved.
    1241             :     //                      ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine
    1242             :     //                              the estimates for integral and error are
    1243             :     //                              less reliable. it is assumed that the
    1244             :     //                              requested accuracy has not been achieved.
    1245             :     //             error messages
    1246             :     //                          = 1 maximum number of subdivisions allowed
    1247             :     //                              has been achieved. one can allow more sub-
    1248             :     //                              divisions by increasing the value of limit
    1249             :     //                              (and taking the according dimension
    1250             :     //                              adjustments into account). however, if
    1251             :     //                              this yields no improvement it is advised
    1252             :     //                              to analyze the integrand in order to
    1253             :     //                              determine the integration difficulties. if
    1254             :     //                              the position of a local difficulty can be
    1255             :     //                              determined (e.g. singularity,
    1256             :     //                              discontinuity within the interval) one
    1257             :     //                              will probably gain from splitting up the
    1258             :     //                              interval at this point and calling the
    1259             :     //                              integrator on the subranges. if possible,
    1260             :     //                              an appropriate special-purpose integrator
    1261             :     //                              should be used, which is designed for
    1262             :     //                              handling the type of difficulty involved.
    1263             :     //                          = 2 the occurrence of roundoff error is detec-
    1264             :     //                              ted, which prevents the requested
    1265             :     //                              tolerance from being achieved.
    1266             :     //                              the error may be under-estimated.
    1267             :     //                          = 3 extremely bad integrand behaviour
    1268             :     //                              occurs at some points of the integration
    1269             :     //                              interval.
    1270             :     //                          = 4 the algorithm does not converge.
    1271             :     //                              roundoff error is detected in the
    1272             :     //                              extrapolation table.
    1273             :     //                              it is presumed that the requested
    1274             :     //                              tolerance cannot be achieved, and that the
    1275             :     //                              returned result is the best which can be
    1276             :     //                              obtained.
    1277             :     //                          = 5 the integral is probably divergent, or
    1278             :     //                              slowly convergent. it must be noted that
    1279             :     //                              divergence can occur with any other value
    1280             :     //                              of ier.
    1281             :     //                          = 6 the input is invalid, because
    1282             :     //                              epsabs.le.0 and
    1283             :     //                              epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28).
    1284             :     //                              result, abserr, neval, last, rlist(1),
    1285             :     //                              iord(1) and elist(1) are set to zero.
    1286             :     //                              alist(1) and blist(1) are set to a and b
    1287             :     //                              respectively.
    1288             :     //
    1289             :     //             alist  - double precision
    1290             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1291             :     //                       last  elements of which are the left end points
    1292             :     //                      of the subintervals in the partition of the
    1293             :     //                      given integration range (a,b)
    1294             :     //
    1295             :     //             blist  - double precision
    1296             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1297             :     //                       last  elements of which are the right end points
    1298             :     //                      of the subintervals in the partition of the given
    1299             :     //                      integration range (a,b)
    1300             :     //
    1301             :     //             rlist  - double precision
    1302             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1303             :     //                       last  elements of which are the integral
    1304             :     //                      approximations on the subintervals
    1305             :     //
    1306             :     //             elist  - double precision
    1307             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1308             :     //                       last  elements of which are the moduli of the
    1309             :     //                      absolute error estimates on the subintervals
    1310             :     //
    1311             :     //             iord   - integer
    1312             :     //                      vector of dimension at least limit, the first k
    1313             :     //                      elements of which are pointers to the
    1314             :     //                      error estimates over the subintervals,
    1315             :     //                      such that elist(iord(1)), ..., elist(iord(k))
    1316             :     //                      form a decreasing sequence, with k = last
    1317             :     //                      if last.le.(limit/2+2), and k = limit+1-last
    1318             :     //                      otherwise
    1319             :     //
    1320             :     //             last   - integer
    1321             :     //                      number of subintervals actually produced in the
    1322             :     //                      subdivision process
    1323             :     //
    1324             :     // ***references  (none)
    1325             :     // ***routines called  d1mach,dqelg,dqk21,dqpsrt
    1326             :     // ***end prologue  dqagse
    1327             :     //
    1328             :     //
    1329             :     //             the dimension of rlist2 is determined by the value of
    1330             :     //             limexp in subroutine dqelg (rlist2 should be of dimension
    1331             :     //             (limexp+2) at least).
    1332             :     //
    1333             :     //             list of major variables
    1334             :     //             -----------------------
    1335             :     //
    1336             :     //            alist     - list of left end points of all subintervals
    1337             :     //                        considered up to now
    1338             :     //            blist     - list of right end points of all subintervals
    1339             :     //                        considered up to now
    1340             :     //            rlist(i)  - approximation to the integral over
    1341             :     //                        (alist(i),blist(i))
    1342             :     //            rlist2    - array of dimension at least limexp+2 containing
    1343             :     //                        the part of the epsilon table which is still

    1611             : void
    1612           1 : dqawce(double(*fcn)(double* x), const double a, const double b, const double c,
    1613             :        const double epsabs, const double epsrel, const int limit, double* result,

    1616             : {
    1617             :     // ***begin prologue  dqawce
    1618             :     // ***date written   800101   (yymmdd)
    1619             :     // ***revision date  830518   (yymmdd)
    1620             :     // ***category no.  h2a2a1,j4
    1621             :     // ***keywords  automatic integrator, special-purpose,
    1622             :     //              cauchy principal value, clenshaw-curtis method
    1623             :     // ***author  piessens,robert,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    1624             :     //            de doncker,elise,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    1625             :     // ***  purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a
    1626             :     //               cauchy principal value i = integral of f*w over (a,b)
    1627             :     //               (w(x) = 1/(x-c), (c.ne.a, c.ne.b), hopefully satisfying
    1628             :     //               following claim for accuracy
    1629             :     //               abs(i-result).le.max(epsabs,epsrel*abs(i))
    1630             :     // ***description
    1631             :     //
    1632             :     //         computation of a cauchy principal value
    1633             :     //         standard fortran subroutine
    1634             :     //         double precision version
    1635             :     //
    1636             :     //         parameters
    1637             :     //          on entry
    1638             :     //             f      - double precision
    1639             :     //                      function subprogram defining the integrand
    1640             :     //                      function f(x). the actual name for f needs to be
    1641             :     //                      declared e x t e r n a l in the driver program.
    1642             :     //
    1643             :     //             a      - double precision
    1644             :     //                      lower limit of integration
    1645             :     //
    1646             :     //             b      - double precision
    1647             :     //                      upper limit of integration
    1648             :     //
    1649             :     //             c      - double precision
    1650             :     //                      parameter in the weight function, c.ne.a, c.ne.b
    1651             :     //                      if c = a or c = b, the routine will end with
    1652             :     //                      ier = 6.
    1653             :     //
    1654             :     //             epsabs - double precision
    1655             :     //                      absolute accuracy requested
    1656             :     //             epsrel - double precision
    1657             :     //                      relative accuracy requested
    1658             :     //                      if  epsabs.le.0
    1659             :     //                      and epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
    1660             :     //                      the routine will end with ier = 6.
    1661             :     //
    1662             :     //             limit  - integer
    1663             :     //                      gives an upper bound on the number of subintervals
    1664             :     //                      in the partition of (a,b), limit.ge.1
    1665             :     //
    1666             :     //          on return
    1667             :     //             result - double precision
    1668             :     //                      approximation to the integral
    1669             :     //
    1670             :     //             abserr - double precision
    1671             :     //                      estimate of the modulus of the absolute error,
    1672             :     //                      which should equal or exceed abs(i-result)
    1673             :     //
    1674             :     //             neval  - integer
    1675             :     //                      number of integrand evaluations
    1676             :     //
    1677             :     //             ier    - integer
    1678             :     //                      ier = 0 normal and reliable termination of the
    1679             :     //                              routine. it is assumed that the requested
    1680             :     //                              accuracy has been achieved.
    1681             :     //                      ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine
    1682             :     //                              the estimates for integral and error are
    1683             :     //                              less reliable. it is assumed that the
    1684             :     //                              requested accuracy has not been achieved.
    1685             :     //             error messages
    1686             :     //                      ier = 1 maximum number of subdivisions allowed
    1687             :     //                              has been achieved. one can allow more sub-
    1688             :     //                              divisions by increasing the value of
    1689             :     //                              limit. however, if this yields no
    1690             :     //                              improvement it is advised to analyze the
    1691             :     //                              the integrand, in order to determine the
    1692             :     //                              the integration difficulties. if the
    1693             :     //                              position of a local difficulty can be
    1694             :     //                              determined (e.g. singularity,
    1695             :     //                              discontinuity within the interval) one
    1696             :     //                              will probably gain from splitting up the
    1697             :     //                              interval at this point and calling
    1698             :     //                              appropriate integrators on the subranges.
    1699             :     //                          = 2 the occurrence of roundoff error is detec-
    1700             :     //                              ted, which prevents the requested
    1701             :     //                              tolerance from being achieved.
    1702             :     //                          = 3 extremely bad integrand behaviour
    1703             :     //                              occurs at some interior points of
    1704             :     //                              the integration interval.
    1705             :     //                          = 6 the input is invalid, because
    1706             :     //                              c = a or c = b or
    1707             :     //                              (epsabs.le.0 and

    1715             :     //             alist   - double precision
    1716             :     //                       vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1717             :     //                        last  elements of which are the left
    1718             :     //                       end points of the subintervals in the partition
    1719             :     //                       of the given integration range (a,b)

    1727             :     //             rlist   - double precision
    1728             :     //                       vector of dimension at least limit, the first
    1729             :     //                        last  elements of which are the integral
    1730             :     //                       approximations on the subintervals
    1731             :     //
    1732             :     //             elist   - double precision
    1733             :     //                       vector of dimension limit, the first  last
    1734             :     //                       elements of which are the moduli of the absolute
    1735             :     //                       error estimates on the subintervals
    1736             :     //
    1737             :     //             iord    - integer
    1738             :     //                       vector of dimension at least limit, the first k
    1739             :     //                       elements of which are pointers to the error
    1740             :     //                       estimates over the subintervals, so that
    1741             :     //                       elist(iord(1)), ..., elist(iord(k)) with k = last
    1742             :     //                       if last.le.(limit/2+2), and k = limit+1-last
    1743             :     //                       otherwise, form a decreasing sequence
    1744             :     //
    1745             :     //             last    - integer

    1752             :     //
    1753             :     //             list of major variables

    1758             :     //            blist     - list of right end points of all subintervals

    1769             :     //                        abs(result))

    1773             :     //

    1777             :     //

    1780             :     //
    1781           1 :     int iroff1, iroff2, k, krule, L, maxerr, nev, nrmax;

    1934             :     // ***purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a
    1935             :     //             given fourier integal
    1936             :     //             i = integral of f(x)*w(x) over (a,infinity)
    1937             :     //             where w(x)=cos(omega*x) or w(x)=sin(omega*x),

    1939             :     //             abs(i-result).le.epsabs.

    1946             :     //         parameters

    2000             :     //                      ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine. the
    2001             :     //                              estimates for integral and error are less
    2002             :     //                              reliable. it is assumed that the requested
    2003             :     //                              accuracy has not been achieved.
    2004             :     //             error messages
    2005             :     //                     if omega.ne.0
    2006             :     //                      ier = 1 maximum number of  cycles  allowed
    2007             :     //                              has been achieved., i.e. of subintervals
    2008             :     //                              (a+(k-1)c,a+kc) where
    2009             :     //                              c = (2*int(abs(omega))+1)*pi/abs(omega),
    2010             :     //                              for k = 1, 2, ..., lst.
    2011             :     //                              one can allow more cycles by increasing
    2012             :     //                              the value of limlst (and taking the
    2013             :     //                              according dimension adjustments into
    2014             :     //                              account).
    2015             :     //                              examine the array iwork which contains
    2016             :     //                              the error flags on the cycles, in order to
    2017             :     //                              look for eventual local integration
    2018             :     //                              difficulties. if the position of a local
    2019             :     //                              difficulty can be determined (e.g.
    2020             :     //                              singularity, discontinuity within the
    2021             :     //                              interval) one will probably gain from
    2022             :     //                              splitting up the interval at this point

    2031             :     //                              array iwork which contains the error
    2032             :     //                              flags on the cycles.
    2033             :     //                          = 6 the input is invalid because

    2044             :     //                              ierlst(k) = 1 the maximum number of

    2800        2089 : dqawse(double(*fcn)(double* x), const double a, const double b, const double alfa,

    2806             :     // ***begin prologue  dqawse
    2807             :     // ***date written   800101   (yymmdd)
    2808             :     // ***revision date  830518   (yymmdd)
    2809             :     // ***category no.  h2a2a1

    2812             :     //              clenshaw-curtis method
    2813             :     // ***author  piessens,robert,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    2814             :     //            de doncker,elise,appl. math. & progr. div. - k.u.leuven
    2815             :     // ***purpose  the routine calculates an approximation result to a given
    2816             :     //             definite integral i = integral of f*w over (a,b),
    2817             :     //             (where w shows a singular behaviour at the end points,
    2818             :     //             see parameter integr).
    2819             :     //             hopefully satisfying following claim for accuracy
    2820             :     //             abs(i-result).le.max(epsabs,epsrel*abs(i)).
    2821             :     // ***description
    2822             :     //
    2823             :     //         integration of functions having algebraico-logarithmic
    2824             :     //         end point singularities
    2825             :     //         standard fortran subroutine
    2826             :     //         double precision version
    2827             :     //
    2828             :     //         parameters
    2829             :     //          on entry
    2830             :     //             f      - double precision
    2831             :     //                      function subprogram defining the integrand
    2832             :     //                      function f(x). the actual name for f needs to be
    2833             :     //                      declared e x t e r n a l in the driver program.
    2834             :     //
    2835             :     //             a      - double precision
    2836             :     //                      lower limit of integration
    2837             :     //
    2838             :     //             b      - double precision
    2839             :     //                      upper limit of integration, b.gt.a
    2840             :     //                      if b.le.a, the routine will end with ier = 6.
    2841             :     //
    2842             :     //             alfa   - double precision
    2843             :     //                      parameter in the weight function, alfa.gt.(-1)
    2844             :     //                      if alfa.le.(-1), the routine will end with
    2845             :     //                      ier = 6.
    2846             :     //
    2847             :     //             beta   - double precision
    2848             :     //                      parameter in the weight function, beta.gt.(-1)
    2849             :     //                      if beta.le.(-1), the routine will end with
    2850             :     //                      ier = 6.
    2851             :     //
    2852             :     //             integr - integer
    2853             :     //                      indicates which weight function is to be used
    2854             :     //                      = 1  (x-a)**alfa*(b-x)**beta
    2855             :     //                      = 2  (x-a)**alfa*(b-x)**beta*log(x-a)
    2856             :     //                      = 3  (x-a)**alfa*(b-x)**beta*log(b-x)
    2857             :     //                      = 4  (x-a)**alfa*(b-x)**beta*log(x-a)*log(b-x)
    2858             :     //                      if integr.lt.1 or integr.gt.4, the routine
    2859             :     //                      will end with ier = 6.
    2860             :     //
    2861             :     //             epsabs - double precision
    2862             :     //                      absolute accuracy requested
    2863             :     //             epsrel - double precision
    2864             :     //                      relative accuracy requested
    2865             :     //                      if  epsabs.le.0
    2866             :     //                      and epsrel.lt.max(50*rel.mach.acc.,0.5d-28),
    2867             :     //                      the routine will end with ier = 6.
    2868             :     //
    2869             :     //             limit  - integer
    2870             :     //                      gives an upper bound on the number of subintervals
    2871             :     //                      in the partition of (a,b), limit.ge.2
    2872             :     //                      if limit.lt.2, the routine will end with ier = 6.
    2873             :     //
    2874             :     //          on return

    2876             :     //                      approximation to the integral
    2877             :     //
    2878             :     //             abserr - double precision
    2879             :     //                      estimate of the modulus of the absolute error,
    2880             :     //                      which should equal or exceed abs(i-result)
    2881             :     //
    2882             :     //             neval  - integer
    2883             :     //                      number of integrand evaluations
    2884             :     //
    2885             :     //             ier    - integer
    2886             :     //                      ier = 0 normal and reliable termination of the
    2887             :     //                              routine. it is assumed that the requested
    2888             :     //                              accuracy has been achieved.
    2889             :     //                      ier.gt.0 abnormal termination of the routine
    2890             :     //                              the estimates for the integral and error
    2891             :     //                              are less reliable. it is assumed that the
    2892             :     //                              requested accuracy has not been achieved.
    2893             :     //             error messages
    2894             :     //                          = 1 maximum number of subdivisions allowed
    2895             :     //                              has been achieved. one can allow more
    2896             :     //                              subdivisions by increasing the value of
    2897             :     //                              limit. however, if this yields no
    2898             :     //                              improvement, it is advised to analyze the
    2899             :     //                              integrand in order to determine the
    2900             :     //                              integration difficulties which prevent the
    2901             :     //                              requested tolerance from being achieved.
    2902             :     //                              in case of a jump discontinuity or a local
    2903             :     //                              singularity of algebraico-logarithmic type
    2904             :     //                              at one or more interior points of the
    2905             :     //                              integration range, one should proceed by
    2906             :     //                              splitting up the interval at these

    4297             :     //             approximations, by means of the epsilon algorithm of
    4298             :     //             p.wynn. an estimate of the absolute error is also given.

    4300             :     //             elements needed for the computation of the next diagonal

    4315             :     //                        of the two lower diagonals of the triangular

    4882             :     //                            estimate

    4885             :     //

    4887             :     //            standard fortran subroutine

    4911             :     //

    4913             :     //                        upper limit of integration
    4914             :     //
    4915             :     //             on return
    4916             :     //               result - double precision
    4917             :     //                        approximation to the integral i
    4918             :     //                        result is computed by applying the 15-point
    4919             :     //                        kronrod rule (resk) obtained by optimal addition
    4920             :     //                        of abscissae to the 7-point gauss rule (resg).
